<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">April 2015 Nepal earthquake</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>

<th scope="row">Aftershocks</th>

6.7 M<sub>w</sub> on 26 April at 12:54<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthquake.usgs.gov_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-earthquake.usgs.gov-4">[4]</a></sup><br/>

</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Casualties</th>
<td>
<p>8,857 dead in Nepal and 8,964 in total<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drrportal_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-drrportal-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D2015_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-D2015-7">[7]</a></sup> 21,952 injured <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drrportal_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-drrportal-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
3.5 million homeless <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drrportal_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-drrportal-6">[6]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>April 2015 Nepal earthquake</b> (also known as the <b>Gorkha earthquake</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSC_Nepal_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_Nepal-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> killed nearly 9,000 people and injured nearly 22,000. It occurred at <time datetime="2015-04-25 11:26"><abbr title="06:11:26 UTC; NST—Nepal Standard Time">11:56 Nepal Standard Time</abbr></time> on 25 April, with a magnitude of 7.8<a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">M<sub>w</sub></a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup> or 8.1<a href="/wiki/Surface_wave_magnitude" title="Surface wave magnitude">M<sub>s</sub></a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CENC_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-CENC-9">[9]</a></sup> and a maximum <a href="/wiki/Mercalli_intensity_scale" title="Mercalli intensity scale">Mercalli Intensity</a> of IX (<i>Violent</i>). Its <a href="/wiki/Epicenter" title="Epicenter">epicenter</a> was east of <a href="/wiki/Gorkha_District" title="Gorkha District">Gorkha District</a> at Barpak, Gorkha, and its <a href="/wiki/Hypocenter" title="Hypocenter">hypocenter</a> was at a depth of approximately 8.2 km (5.1 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup> It was the worst natural disaster to strike <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> since the <a href="/wiki/1934_Nepal%E2%80%93Bihar_earthquake" title="1934 Nepal–Bihar earthquake">1934 Nepal–Bihar earthquake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indianexpress.com_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-indianexpress.com-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The ground motion recorded in Kathmandu valley was of low frequency which, along with its occurrence at an hour where many people in rural areas were working outdoors, decreased the loss of property and human life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earthquake triggered <a href="/wiki/2015_Mount_Everest_avalanches" title="2015 Mount Everest avalanches">an avalanche on Mount Everest</a>, killing 21,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> making April 25, 2015 the deadliest day on the mountain in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The earthquake triggered another huge avalanche in the <a href="/wiki/Langtang" title="Langtang">Langtang</a> valley, where 250 people were reported missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langtang_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Langtang-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MailOnline_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-MailOnline-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hundreds of thousands of people were made homeless with entire villages flattened,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langtang_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Langtang-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MontanaPublicRadio_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-MontanaPublicRadio-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barpak_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barpak-19">[19]</a></sup> across many districts of the country. Centuries-old buildings were destroyed at UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage sites</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">Kathmandu Valley</a>, including some at the <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square" title="Kathmandu Durbar Square">Kathmandu Durbar Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Patan_Durbar_Square" title="Patan Durbar Square">Patan Durbar Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bhaktapur_Durbar_Square" title="Bhaktapur Durbar Square">Bhaktapur Durbar Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Changu_Narayan" title="Changu Narayan">Changu Narayan</a> Temple, the <a href="/wiki/Boudhanath" title="Boudhanath">Boudhanath</a> stupa and the <a href="/wiki/Swayambhunath" title="Swayambhunath">Swayambhunath</a> Stupa. Geophysicists and other experts had warned for decades that Nepal was vulnerable to a deadly earthquake, particularly because of its geology, urbanization, and architecture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Continued <a href="/wiki/Aftershock" title="Aftershock">aftershocks</a> occurred throughout Nepal at the intervals of 15–20 minutes, with one shock reaching a magnitude of 6.7 on 26 April at <time datetime="2015-04-25 12:54">12:54:08</time> <a href="/wiki/Nepal_Standard_Time" title="Nepal Standard Time">NST</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthquake.usgs.gov_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-earthquake.usgs.gov-4">[4]</a></sup> The country also had a continued risk of landslides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/May_2015_Nepal_earthquake" title="May 2015 Nepal earthquake">A major aftershock</a> occurred on 12 May 2015 at <time datetime="2015-05-12 12:35"><abbr title="07:05 UTC; NST—Nepal Standard Time">12:50 NST</abbr></time> with a <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">moment magnitude</a> (M<sub>w</sub>) of 7.3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Earthquake_again_in_Nepal_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Earthquake_again_in_Nepal-23">[23]</a></sup> The epicenter was near the Chinese border between the capital of Kathmandu and Mt. Everest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> More than 200 people were killed and more than 2,500 were injured by this aftershock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN2nd_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN2nd-25">[25]</a></sup></p>

</li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Damage"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Damage</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquake">Earthquake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Earthquake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NepalAftershockMap.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="573" data-file-width="640" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NepalAftershockMap.png/280px-NepalAftershockMap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NepalAftershockMap.png/420px-NepalAftershockMap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/NepalAftershockMap.png/560px-NepalAftershockMap.png 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NepalAftershockMap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the earthquake and aftershocks at 12 May, showing location of major historical earthquakes</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The earthquake occurred on 25 April 2015 at <time datetime="2015-04-25 11:56">11:56 a.m.</time> <a href="/wiki/Nepal_Standard_Time" title="Nepal Standard Time">NST</a> (06:11:26 UTC) at a depth of approximately 15 km (9.3 mi) (which is considered shallow and therefore more damaging than quakes that originate deeper in the ground),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-26">[26]</a></sup> with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epicentre" title="Epicentre">epicentre</a> approximately 34 km (21 mi) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Lamjung_District" title="Lamjung District">Lamjung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, lasting approximately fifty seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alj_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-alj-27">[27]</a></sup> The earthquake was initially reported as 7.5 M<sub>w</sub> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> (USGS) before it was quickly upgraded to 7.8 M<sub>w</sub>. The <a href="/wiki/China_Earthquake_Networks_Center" title="China Earthquake Networks Center">China Earthquake Networks Center</a> (CENC) reported the earthquake's magnitude to be 8.1 M<sub>s</sub>. The <a href="/wiki/India_Meteorological_Department" title="India Meteorological Department">India Meteorological Department</a> (IMD) said two powerful quakes were registered in Nepal at 06:11 UTC and 06:45 UTC. The first quake measured 7.8 M<sub>w</sub> and its epicenter was identified at a distance of 80 km to the northwest of <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">Kathmandu</a>, the capital of Nepal. <a href="/wiki/Bharatpur,_Nepal" title="Bharatpur, Nepal">Bharatpur</a> was the nearest major city to the main earthquake, 53 km (33 mi) from the epicenter. The second earthquake was somewhat less powerful at 6.6 M<sub>w</sub>. It occurred 65 km (40 mi) east of Kathmandu and its seismic focus lay at a depth of 10 km (6.2 mi) below the earth's surface. Over thirty-eight aftershocks of magnitude 4.5 M<sub>w</sub> or greater occurred in the day following the initial earthquake, including the one of magnitude 6.8 M<sub>w</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-earthNP_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-earthNP-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the USGS, the earthquake was caused by a sudden thrust, or release of built-up stress, along the major fault line where the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Plate" title="Indian Plate">Indian Plate</a>, carrying India, is slowly diving underneath the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>, carrying much of Europe and Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-NatGeo-26">[26]</a></sup> Kathmandu, situated on a block of crust approximately 120 km (74 miles) wide and 60 km (37 miles) long, reportedly shifted 3 m (10 ft) to the south in a matter of just 30 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SydMorn_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-SydMorn-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The risk of a large earthquake was well known beforehand. In 2013, in an interview with seismologist Vinod Kumar Gaur, <i>The Hindu</i> quoted him as saying, "Calculations show that there is sufficient accumulated energy [in the <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Nepal#Terai" title="Geology of Nepal">Main Frontal Thrust</a>], now to produce an 8 magnitude earthquake. I cannot say when. It may not happen tomorrow, but it could possibly happen sometime this century, or wait longer to produce a much larger one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> According to Brian Tucker, founder of a nonprofit organization devoted to reducing casualties from natural disasters, some government officials had expressed confidence that such an earthquake would not occur again. Tucker recounted a conversation he had had with a government official in the 1990s who said, "We don't have to worry about earthquakes anymore, because we already had an earthquake"; the previous earthquake to which he referred occurred in 1934.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1723" data-file-width="2658" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png/240px-Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png/360px-Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png/480px-Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himalayan_Tectonic_Summary.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
M6+ Himalayan region earthquakes, 1900–2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Nepal" title="Geology of Nepal">Geology of Nepal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thrust_tectonics" title="Thrust tectonics">Thrust tectonics</a></div>
<p>Nepal lies towards the southern limit of the diffuse <a href="/wiki/Continental_collision" title="Continental collision">collisional</a> boundary where the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Plate" title="Indian Plate">Indian Plate</a> underthrusts the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> occupying the central sector of the Himalayan arc, nearly one-third of the 2,400 km (1,500 mi) long Himalayas. Geologically, the Nepal Himalayas are sub-divided into five tectonic zones from north to south and, east to west and almost parallel to sub-parallel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> These five distinct morpho-geotectonic zones are: (1) <a href="/wiki/Terai" title="Terai">Terai</a> Plain, (2) Sub Himalaya (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sivalik" title="Sivalik">Sivalik</a> Range), (3) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesser_Himalaya" title="Lesser Himalaya">Lesser Himalaya</a> (Mahabharat Range and mid valleys), (4) Higher Himalaya, and (5) Inner Himalaya (Tibetan Tethys).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_Geology_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nepal_Geology-35">[35]</a></sup> Each of these zones is clearly identified by their morphological, geological, and tectonic features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_Geology_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nepal_Geology-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The convergence rate between the plates in central Nepal is about 45 mm (1.8 in) per year. The location, magnitude, and <a href="/wiki/Focal_mechanism" title="Focal mechanism">focal mechanism</a> of the earthquake suggest that it was caused by a slip along the Main Frontal Thrust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earthquake's effects were amplified in Kathmandu as it sits on the Kathmandu Basin, which contains up to 600 m (2,000 ft) of <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a>, representing the infilling of a lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mugnier_et_al_2011_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mugnier_et_al_2011-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Based on a study published in 2014, of the Main Frontal Thrust, on average a great earthquake occurs every 750 ± 140 and 870 ± 350 years in the east Nepal region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> A study from 2015 found a 700-year delay between earthquakes in the region. The study also suggests that because of tectonic stress buildup, the earthquake from 1934 in Nepal and the 2015 quake are connected, following a historic earthquake pattern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> A 2016 study on historical great (M ≥ 8) earthquake pairs and cycles found that associated great earthquakes are likely to occur in West China region through the 2020s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West_China_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-West_China-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intensity">Intensity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Intensity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2157" data-file-width="3425" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png/240px-Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png/360px-Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png/480px-Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gorkha_isoseismal_map_USGS_annotated.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Isoseismal_map" title="Isoseismal map">Isoseismal map</a> for the Gorkha earthquake annotated with values on the <a href="/wiki/Mercalli_intensity_scale" title="Mercalli intensity scale">Mercalli intensity scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to "Did You Feel It?" (DYFI?) responses on the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">USGS</a> website, the intensity in small parts of Kathmandu was IX (<i>Violent</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup> In most of Kathmandu the intensity was VI, as evidenced by the numerous undamaged water towers installed on top of undamaged multi story buildings. Tremors were felt in the neighboring Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">Sikkim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand" title="Uttarakhand">Uttarakhand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2015)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in the National capital region around <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)" title="National Capital Region (India)">New Delhi</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> and as far south as <a href="/wiki/Karnataka" title="Karnataka">Karnataka</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (July 2016)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many buildings were brought down in Bihar. Minor cracks in the walls of houses were reported in Odisha. Minor quakes were registered as far as <a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">Kochi</a> in the southern state of <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>. The intensity in <a href="/wiki/Patna" title="Patna">Patna</a> was V (<i>Moderate</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (July 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> The intensity was IV (<i>Light</i>) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhaka,_Bangladesh" title="Dhaka, Bangladesh">Dhaka, Bangladesh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup> The earthquake was also experienced across southwestern <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, which is 1,900 km (1,200 mi) away from the epicenter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Tremors were felt in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hjelmgaard_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hjelmgaard-46">[46]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftershocks">Aftershocks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Aftershocks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_aftershocks_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake" title="List of aftershocks after the 2015 Nepal earthquake">List of aftershocks after the 2015 Nepal earthquake</a></div>
<p>A series of aftershocks began immediately after the mainshock, at intervals of 15–30 minutes, with one aftershock reaching 6.6M<sub>w</sub> within 34 minutes of the initial quake. A major aftershock of magnitude 6.9 M<sub>w</sub> occurred on 26 April 2015 in the same region at 12:54 NST (07:08 UTC), with an epicenter located about 17 km (11 mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Kodari" title="Kodari">Kodari</a>, Nepal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hjelmgaard_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hjelmgaard-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The aftershock caused fresh avalanches on Mount Everest and was felt in many places in northern India including <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">Kolkata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siliguri" title="Siliguri">Siliguri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalpaiguri" title="Jalpaiguri">Jalpaiguri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-48">[48]</a></sup> The aftershock caused a landslide on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Nepal" title="List of roads in Nepal">Koshi Highway</a> which blocked the section of the road between <a href="/wiki/Dharan,_Nepal" title="Dharan, Nepal">Bhedetar</a> and Mulghat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>A model of GeoGateway, based on a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> mechanism of a near-horizontal fault as well as location of aftershocks showed that the fault had an 11° <a href="/wiki/Strike_and_dip" title="Strike and dip">dip</a> towards the north, striking at 295°, 50 km (31 mi) wide, 150 km (93 mi) long, and had a dip slip of 3 m (9.8 ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The USGS says the aftershock registered at a shallow depth of 10 km (6.2 mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Assuming that 25 April earthquake was the largest event in this seismic episode, Nepal could expect more than 30 aftershocks greater than magnitude 5 over the following month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> As of 24 May 2016, 459 aftershocks had occurred with different epicenters and magnitudes equal to or above 4 M<sub>w</sub> (out of which 51 aftershocks are equal to or above 5 M<sub>w</sub> and 5 aftershocks above 6 M<sub>w</sub>) and more than 20,000 aftershocks less than 4 M<sub>w</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSC_Nepal_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_Nepal-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="12_May_2015_earthquake">12 May 2015 earthquake</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 12 May 2015 earthquake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/May_2015_Nepal_earthquake" title="May 2015 Nepal earthquake">May 2015 Nepal earthquake</a></div>
<p>A second major earthquake occurred on 12 May 2015 at 12:50 NST with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude" title="Moment magnitude">moment magnitude</a> (M<sub>w</sub>) of 7.3M<sub>w</sub> 18 km (11 mi) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Kodari" title="Kodari">Kodari</a>. The epicenter was near the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> border between the capital of <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">Kathmandu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Everest" title="Mt. Everest">Mt. Everest</a>. It struck at the depth of 18.5 km (11.5 miles). This earthquake occurred along the same fault as the original magnitude 7.8 earthquake of 25 April but further to the east. As such, it is considered to be an <a href="/wiki/Aftershock" title="Aftershock">aftershock</a> of the 25 April quake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USGS_Desc_2_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Desc_2-52">[52]</a></sup> Tremors were also felt in northern parts of India including <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bengal" title="West Bengal">West Bengal</a> and other North-Indian States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> At least 153 died in Nepal as a result of the aftershock and about 2,500 were injured. 62 others died in India, two in Bangladesh, and one in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN2nd_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN2nd-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNclimbs_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNclimbs-56">[56]</a></sup> In Kathmandu the intensity was VI. People ran out of doors, or dove under a strong table (a behaviour more recommended), but water towers on top of multi story buildings remained intact.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%932016_Nepal_humanitarian_crisis" title="2015–2016 Nepal humanitarian crisis">2015–2016 Nepal humanitarian crisis</a></div>
<p>Disastrous events in very poor and politically paralyzed nations such as Nepal often become <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_effect" title="Butterfly effect">a long drawn out chain of events</a>, in that one disaster feeds into another for years or even decades upon end. The aftereffects from the earthquake have knock-on effects on a myriad of seemingly unrelated aspects: <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Employment" title="Employment">labour</a> cost and availability, rental and property cost burdens, <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a>, private and public debt burdens, mental health, politics, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, disease, and damage to the healthcare system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some disasters that came with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monsoon_season" title="Monsoon season">monsoon season</a> were suspected to be related to the earthquake. There was a landslip on 11 June that claimed 53 lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Meanwhile, a glacial lake had burst in particularly hard hit Solukhumbhu district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Whether or not the quake had contributed to such events is often unknown and unresearched, but certainly possible.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Nepal</dt>
</dl>
<p>The earthquake killed more than 8,800 in Nepal<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drrportal_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-drrportal-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and injured nearly three times as many. The rural death toll may have been minimized by the fact that most villagers were outdoors working when the quake hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> As of 15 May, 6,271 people, including 1,700 from the 12 May aftershock, were still receiving treatment for their injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNclimbs_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNNclimbs-56">[56]</a></sup> Nearly 3.5 million people were left homeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoHA_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-MoHA-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Himalayan_Times" title="The Himalayan Times">The Himalayan Times</a></i> reported that as many as 20,000 foreign nationals may have been visiting Nepal at the time of the earthquake, although reports of foreign deaths were relatively low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>India</dt>
</dl>
<p>A total of 78 deaths were reported in India - including 58 in Bihar, 16 in Uttar Pradesh, 3 in West Bengal and 1 in Rajasthan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zee_India_Toll_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zee_India_Toll-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>China</dt>
</dl>
<p>27 dead and 4 missing, all from the <a href="/wiki/Tibet_Autonomous_Region" title="Tibet Autonomous Region">Tibet Autonomous Region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Xinhua_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Bangladesh</dt>
</dl>
<p>4 dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bdnews24.com_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bdnews24.com-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Avalanches_on_Mount_Everest">Avalanches on Mount Everest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Avalanches on Mount Everest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2015_Mount_Everest_avalanches" title="2015 Mount Everest avalanches">2015 Mount Everest avalanches</a></div>
<p>This earthquake caused <a href="/wiki/Avalanche" title="Avalanche">avalanches</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">Mount Everest</a>. At least 19 died,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAPOeyes_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-WAPOeyes-90">[90]</a></sup> including Google executive <a href="/wiki/Dan_Fredinburg" title="Dan Fredinburg">Dan Fredinburg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> with at least 120 others injured or missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAPOeyes_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-WAPOeyes-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Landslides_in_the_Langtang_Valley">Landslides in the Langtang Valley</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Landslides in the Langtang Valley">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Langtang" title="Langtang">Langtang valley</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Langtang_National_Park" title="Langtang National Park">Langtang National Park</a>, 329 people were reported missing after an avalanche hit the village of Ghodatabela<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Langtang,_Bagmati" title="Langtang, Bagmati">village of Langtang</a>. The avalanche was estimated to have been two to three kilometres wide. Ghodatabela was an area popular on the Langtang trekking route.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The village of Langtang was destroyed by the avalanche. Smaller settlements on the outskirts of Langtang were buried during the earthquake, such as Chyamki, Thangsyap, and Mundu. Twelve locals and two foreigners were believed to have survived. Smaller <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a> occurred in the <a href="/wiki/Trishuli_River" title="Trishuli River">Trishuli River</a> Valley with reports of significant damage at Mailung, Simle, and <a href="/wiki/Archale" title="Archale">Archale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MailOnline_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-MailOnline-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> On 4 May it was announced that 52 bodies had been found in the Langtang area, of which seven were of foreigners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to geological models, the frequency and intensity of future landslides in the Langtang Valley is due to increase in the coming decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> This is attributable directly to the effect of the earthquake, which caused widespread fracturing in the grounds of the Langtang area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Damage">Damage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Damage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26,_2015.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG/220px-Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG/330px-Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG/440px-Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26%2C_2015.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Airways_Cargo_B777_providing_humanitarian_support_after_the_2015_Nepal_earthquake_April_26,_2015.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Travellers waiting on airport tarmac for flights after aftershocks forced the airport to open all exit doors.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG/220px-Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG/330px-Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG/440px-Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Durbarsquare_after_earthquake_3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage in the Basantpur Durbar Square.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thousands of houses were destroyed across many districts of the country, with entire villages flattened, especially those near the epicenter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langtang_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Langtang-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MontanaPublicRadio_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-MontanaPublicRadio-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barpak_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barpak-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tribhuvan_International_Airport" title="Tribhuvan International Airport">Tribhuvan International Airport</a> serving Kathmandu was closed immediately after the quake, but was re-opened later in the day for relief operations and, later, for some commercial flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> It subsequently shut down operations sporadically due to aftershocks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and on 3 May was closed temporarily to the largest planes for fear of runway damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> During strong aftershocks, the airport opened all boarding-lounge exit doors onto the tarmac, allowing travelers who were waiting post security and immigration to flee to the open spaces of the runway tarmac. Many travelers remained outside as planes were delayed and the airport swelled to capacity. The airport facilities suffered damage and there was no running water or operating toilets for travelers waiting in the airport lounges. Few airport workers were at their posts; most were killed in the earthquake or had to deal with its aftereffects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Flights resumed from Pokhara, to the west of the epicentre, on 27 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:164px;max-width:164px">
<div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square" title="Kathmandu Durbar Square">Kathmandu Durbar Square</a></div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kathmandu_Durbar_Square,_Nepal.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="598" data-file-width="900" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG/160px-Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG/240px-Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG/320px-Kathmandu_Durbar_Square%2C_Nepal.JPG 2x" width="160"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Before the earthquake</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg/240px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg/360px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg/480px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_Earthquake_2015_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Building damage as a result of the earthquake</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several of the churches in the Kathmandu valley were destroyed. As Saturday is the principal day of Christian worship in Nepal, 500 people were reported to have died in the collapses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Temple" title="Temple">temples</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Durbar_Square" title="Kathmandu Durbar Square">Kathmandu Durbar Square</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, collapsed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alj_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-alj-27">[27]</a></sup> as did the <a href="/wiki/Dharahara" title="Dharahara">Dharahara</a> tower, built in 1832; the collapse of the latter structure killed at least 180 people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manakamana" title="Manakamana">Manakamana</a> Temple in Gorkha, previously damaged in an earlier quake, tilted several inches further. The northern side of <a href="/wiki/Janaki_Mandir" title="Janaki Mandir">Janaki Mandir</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Janakpur" title="Janakpur">Janakpur</a> was reported to have been damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Several temples, including <a href="/wiki/Kasthamandap" title="Kasthamandap">Kasthamandap</a>, Panchtale temple, the top levels of the nine-story Basantapur Durbar, the Dasa Avtar temple and two dewals located behind the Shiva Parvati temple were demolished by the quake. Some other monuments including the Taleju Bhawani Temple partially collapsed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-naturaldisasters1_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-naturaldisasters1-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg/220px-Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg/330px-Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg/440px-Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gorkha_Earthquake_Effect.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged building Around Balaju Area due to Earthquake in April 25, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The top of the Jaya Bageshwari Temple in Gaushala and some parts of the <a href="/wiki/Pashupatinath_Temple" title="Pashupatinath Temple">Pashupatinath Temple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swyambhunath" title="Swyambhunath">Swyambhunath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boudhanath" title="Boudhanath">Boudhanath</a> Stupa, Ratna Mandir, inside Rani Pokhari, and <a href="/wiki/Durbar_High_School" title="Durbar High School">Durbar High School</a> have been destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Patan, the Char Narayan Mandir, the statue of Yog Narendra Malla, a pati inside Patan Durbar Square, the Taleju Temple, the Hari Shankar, Uma Maheshwar Temple and the Machhindranath Temple in Bungamati were destroyed. In Tripureshwar, the Kal Mochan Ghat, a temple inspired by Mughal architecture, was completely destroyed and the nearby Tripura Sundari also suffered significant damage. In Bhaktapur, several monuments, including the Phasi Deva temple, the Chardham temple and the 17th century Vatsala Durga Temple were fully or partially destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>Outside the Valley, the <a href="/wiki/Manakamana" title="Manakamana">Manakamana</a> Temple in Gorkha, the Gorkha Durbar, the Palanchok Bhagwati, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kavrepalanchowk_District" title="Kavrepalanchowk District">Kabhrepalanchok District</a>, the Rani Mahal in <a href="/wiki/Palpa_District" title="Palpa District">Palpa District</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Churiyamai" title="Churiyamai">Churiyamai</a> in <a href="/wiki/Makwanpur_District" title="Makwanpur District">Makwanpur District</a>, the Dolakha Bhimsensthan in <a href="/wiki/Dolakha_District" title="Dolakha District">Dolakha District</a>, and the Nuwakot Durbar suffered varying degrees of damage. Historian Prushottam Lochan Shrestha stated, "We have lost most of the monuments that had been designated as World Heritage Sites in <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">Kathmandu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhaktapur" title="Bhaktapur">Bhaktapur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lalitpur_District,_Nepal" title="Lalitpur District, Nepal">Lalitpur District, Nepal</a>. They cannot be restored to their original states."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-114">[114]</a></sup> The northeastern parts of India also received major damage. Heavy shocks were felt in the states of Uttrakhand, Uttar Pradesh, West Bengal and others. Huge damage was caused to the property and the lives of the people.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_loss">Economic loss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economic loss">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg/240px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg/360px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg/480px-Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_Earthquake_2015_08.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Road damage in Nepal</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Concern was expressed that harvests could be reduced or lost this season as people affected by the earthquake would have only a short time to plant crops before the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">Monsoon</a> rains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nepal, with a total Gross Domestic Product of USD$19.921 billion (according to a 2012 estimate),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> is one of Asia's poorest countries, and has little ability to fund a major reconstruction effort on its own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_Business_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_Business-117">[117]</a></sup> Even before the quake, the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> estimated that it would need to spend about four times more than it currently does annually on infrastructure through to 2020 to attract investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_Business_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_Business-117">[117]</a></sup> The U.S. Geological Survey initially estimated economic losses from the tremor at 9 percent to 50 percent of gross domestic product, with a best guess of 35 percent. "It’s too hard for now to tell the extent of the damage and the effect on Nepal’s GDP", according to Hun Kim, an Asian Development Bank (ADB) official. The ADB said on the 28th that it would provide a USD$3 million grant to Nepal for immediate relief efforts, and up to USD$200 million for the first phase of rehabilitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_Business_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_Business-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka,Nepal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="446" data-file-width="576" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg/240px-Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg/360px-Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg/480px-Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka%2CNepal.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Broken_House_at_Chaurikharka,Nepal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damaged house in <a href="/wiki/Chaurikharka" title="Chaurikharka">Chaurikharka</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rajiv Biswas, an economist at a <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>-based consultancy, said that rebuilding the economy will need international effort over the next few years as it could "easily exceed" USD$5 billion, or about 20 percent of Nepal's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_Business_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_Business-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-times-herald.com_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-times-herald.com-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="only part of this quotation is found in the sources (May 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_effects">Social effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Social effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It was reported that the survivors were preyed upon by human traffickers involved in the supply of girls and women to the brothels of South Asia. These traffickers took advantage of the chaos that resulted from the aftermath of the earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burke5May2015_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burke5May2015-119">[119]</a></sup> The most affected were women from poor communities who lost their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNWorkers_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNWorkers-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_affected">Most affected</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Most affected">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Single women have had very little access to relief, according to a report by the Inter-party Women’s Alliance (IPWA). The report also found that violence and rapes against women and minors has increased after the earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Additionally, the earthquake has significantly affected certain groups of people. Tibeto-Burman peoples were hardest hit as they tend to inhabit the higher slopes of mountains as opposed to the central valleys, are less educated and connected. All of these factors make them harder to access. According to a government survey, malnutrition in children has worsened considerably some 3 months after the quake, with the most undernourished being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamang" title="Tamang">Tamang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chepang_people" title="Chepang people">Chepang</a> peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malnutrition_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-malnutrition-122">[122]</a></sup> Before the quake, 41 percent of children under five were stunted, 29 percent were underweight and 11 percent were emaciated, according to the World Food Programme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-malnutrition_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-malnutrition-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 3 May, the hashtag #GoHomeIndianMedia was trending worldwide on Twitter, condemning news covered by the Indian media as insensitive and inhumane to victims of the tragedy. The people of Nepal acknowledged the aid and effort put by the Indian armed forces, yet, at the same time, accused Indian news networks of carrying out "a public relations exercise" on behalf of the Indian government, of overemphasizing the role of the Indian Army, and of hogging space on relief planes where aid material or rescue or medical personnel could have been sent instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Indian users responded with the hashtags <i>#SorryNepal</i> and <i>#DontComeBackIndianMedia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disease">Disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though a feared mass cholera outbreak failed to materialize (there were sporadic reports), other outbreaks have been reported. At least 13 people have died of <a href="/wiki/Scrub_typhus" title="Scrub typhus">scrub typhus</a> while 240 people have been taken ill since the disease was first diagnosed in the country in August 2015 until Sept 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rescue_and_relief">Rescue and relief</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rescue and relief">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>About 90% of soldiers from the <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_Army" title="Nepalese Army">Nepalese Army</a> were sent to the stricken areas in the aftermath of the earthquake under <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sankat_Mochan" title="Operation Sankat Mochan">Operation Sankat Mochan</a>, with volunteers mobilized from other parts of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Rainfall and aftershocks were factors complicating the rescue efforts, with potential secondary effects like additional landslides and further building collapses being concerns. Impassable roads and damaged communications infrastructure posed substantial challenges to rescue efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Survivors were found up to a week after the earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ekan-5days_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-ekan-5days-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 1 May international aid agencies like <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="Médecins Sans Frontières">Médecins Sans Frontières</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">Red Cross</a> were able to start medically evacuating the critically wounded by helicopter from outlying areas, initially cut-off from the capital city, Kathmandu,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MontanaPublicRadio_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-MontanaPublicRadio-18">[18]</a></sup> and treating others in mobile and makeshift facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msf29Apr_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-msf29Apr-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-redcross-132">[132]</a></sup> There was concern about epidemics due to the shortage of clean water, the makeshift nature of living conditions and the lack of toilets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Emergency workers were able to identify four men who had been trapped in rubble, and rescue them, using advanced heartbeat detection. The four men were trapped in up to ten feet of rubble in the village of Chautara, north of Kathmandu. An international team of rescuers from several countries using FINDER devices found two sets of men under two different collapsed buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Volunteers used <a href="/wiki/Crisis_mapping" title="Crisis mapping">crisis mapping</a> to help plan emergency aid work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-135">[135]</a></sup> Public volunteers from around the world participated in <a href="/wiki/Crowdmapping" title="Crowdmapping">crowdmapping</a> and added details into online maps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Information was mapped from data input from social media, satellite pictures<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drones</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-135">[135]</a></sup> of passable roads, collapsed houses, stranded, shelterless and starving people, who needed help, and from messages and contact details of people willing to help.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> On-site volunteers verified these mapping details wherever they could to reduce errors. First responders, from Nepalese citizens to the Red Cross, the Nepal army and the United Nations used this data. The Nepal earthquake crisis mapping utilized experience gained and lessons learned about planning emergency aid work from earthquakes in Haiti and Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>India decided to donate $1 billion in cash and materials to Nepal. India's External Affairs Minister Sushma Swaraj said "I am happy to announce Government of India's pledge for Nepal's post-earthquake reconstruction of Nepali Rupees 10,000 crores, equivalent to one billion US dollars, one fourth of it as Grant." The International Conference on Nepal's Reconstruction has been organised by the Nepalese government to raise funds for rebuilding the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Reports are also coming in of sub-standard relief materials and inedible food being sent to Nepal by many of the foreign aid agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> helicopter crashed on 12 May while involved in delivering relief supplies. The <a href="/wiki/Bell_UH-1Y_Venom" title="Bell UH-1Y Venom">Bell UH-1Y Venom</a> crashed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charikot" title="Charikot">Charikot</a>, roughly 45 miles (72 kilometers) east of Kathmandu. Two Nepalese soldiers and 6 American Marines died in the crash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Need-fulfillment application, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Getmii_(app)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Getmii (app) (page does not exist)">Getmii</a>, launched a special pilot version in partnership with the Red Cross to double daily blood donors at the Kathmandu donation center using the app.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Imaging technologies such as satellites and smartphones, were instrumental to relief efforts in Nepal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> GLIMS, group of volunteer scientists from nine nations, were able to provide rapid, systematic mapping of the damaged area, allowing the investigation of earthquake-induced geo-hazard processes which provided information to relief and recovery officials on the same timeframe as those operations were occurring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Repair_and_reconstruction">Repair and reconstruction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Repair and reconstruction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monuments">Monuments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Monuments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UNESCO and the Ministry of Culture began strengthening damaged monuments in danger of collapsing before the monsoon season. Subsequent restoration of collapsed structures, including historic houses is planned. Architectural drawings exist that provide plans for reconstruction. According to UNESCO, more than 30 monuments in the Kathmandu Valley collapsed in the quakes, and another 120 incurred partial damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Repair estimates are $160 million to restore 1,000 damaged and destroyed monasteries, temples, historic houses, and shrines across the country. The destruction is concentrated in the Kathmandu Valley. UNESCO designated seven groups of multi-ethnic monuments clustered in the valley as a single World Heritage Site, including Swayambhu, the Durbar squares of Kathmandu, Patan, and Bhaktapur, and the Hindu temples of Pashupati and Changu Narayan. Damaged in the quakes were the structures in the three Durbar squares, the temple of Changu Narayan, and the 1655 temple in Sankhu. Drones fly above cultural heritage sites to provide 3D images of the damage to use for planning repairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_aid">International aid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=April_2015_Nepal_earthquake&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: International aid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%932017_Nepal_humanitarian_crisis" title="2015–2017 Nepal humanitarian crisis">2015–2017 Nepal humanitarian crisis</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> appealed for donations, as close to 1.7 million children had been driven out into the open, and were in desperate need of drinking water, psychological counsel, temporary shelters, sanitation and protection from disease outbreak. It distributed water, tents, hygiene kits, water purification tablets and buckets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Numerous other organizations provided similar support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>India was the first to respond within hours, being Nepal's immediate neighbour,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Operation_Maitri" title="Operation Maitri">Operation Maitri</a> which provided rescue and relief by its armed forces. It also evacuated its own and other countries' stranded nationals. The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> has been the largest bilateral aid donor to Nepal following the earthquake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The United States, China and other nations have provided helicopters as requested by the Nepalese government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 April 2015, international aid agencies and governments mobilized rescue workers and aid for the earthquake. They faced challenges in both getting assistance to Nepal and ferrying people to remote areas as the country had few helicopters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mark_Scott_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mark_Scott-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TIMEAidAgencies_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-TIMEAidAgencies-163">[163]</a></sup> Relief efforts were also hampered by Nepalese government insistence on routing aid through the Prime Minister's Disaster Relief Fund and its National Emergency Operation Center. After concerns were raised, it was clarified that "Non-profits" or NGOs already in the country could continue receiving aid directly and bypass the official fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mark_Scott_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mark_Scott-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Aid mismatch and supply of "leftovers" by donors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> aid diversion in Nepal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> mistrust over control of the distribution of funds and supplies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> congestion and customs delays at Kathmandu's airport and border check posts were also reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> On 3 May 2015, restrictions were placed on heavy aircraft flying in aid supplies after new cracks were noticed on the runway at the <a href="/wiki/Tribhuvan_International_Airport" title="Tribhuvan International Airport">Tribhuvan airport (KTM)</a>, Nepal's only wide-body jet airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto3_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto4_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>The list below gives a break-up of pledged donations, by each nation, along with aid in kind, delivered immediately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto2_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-175">[175]</a></sup></p>

• Four cargo trucks carrying approximately 25 tonnes of essential relief materials for earthquake victims in Nepal left Dhaka. The cargoes will travel through Banglabandh-Fulbari-Panitanki-Kakarbhitta land route. The relief materials include 3000 cartons (12 tonne) of dry food and fruit juice donated by <a href="/wiki/PRAN" title="PRAN">Pran</a>, and 5000 pieces of blankets donated by <a href="/wiki/BRAC_(NGO)" title="BRAC (NGO)">Brac</a>, according to a press release of the Embassy of Nepal in Bangladesh.<br/>
• Bangladesh will provide at least one hundred thousand tons of rice and other relief materials including drinking water to help the earthquake victims in Nepal.</p>
